  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_05a8b8aa-3f36-4b36-b919-382a170ca1d2'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2307001570" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer16141584877991562185">The pages just flew by and I realized the book was over. However, there was an epilogue that deserved thinking about. Sidney Sheldon is not a perfect writer. But this book of his is so much better than many bestsellers today.<br/><br/>The author has used sex, action, and loneliness tropes to great effect here. Windmill of the Gods is slightly dated, but you can treat it like a classic, if you want.<br/><br/>The violence in the book is sometimes there, and sometimes it's hinted at. The fate of the evil mastermind is</span>
  <span id="freeText16141584877991562185" style="display:none">The pages just flew by and I realized the book was over. However, there was an epilogue that deserved thinking about. Sidney Sheldon is not a perfect writer. But this book of his is so much better than many bestsellers today.<br /><br />The author has used sex, action, and loneliness tropes to great effect here. Windmill of the Gods is slightly dated, but you can treat it like a classic, if you want.<br /><br />The violence in the book is sometimes there, and sometimes it's hinted at. The fate of the evil mastermind is terrible, despite his shenanigans. I won't spoil the story in my review. Read it and be thrilled.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer14930919788902235268">Windmills of the Gods, Sidney Sheldon<br/>Windmills of the Gods is a 1987 thriller novel by American writer Sidney Sheldon. Mary Ashley, a professor at Kansas State University, is offered an ambassadorship by Paul Ellison, the US president. She rejects the offer because her husband, Dr. Edward Ashley, does not want to leave his medical practice, and she is not willing to be separated from him. She also feels that it is harder to find a good doctor for a small Kansas town than an ambassador to a forei</span>
  <span id="freeText14930919788902235268" style="display:none">Windmills of the Gods, Sidney Sheldon<br />Windmills of the Gods is a 1987 thriller novel by American writer Sidney Sheldon. Mary Ashley, a professor at Kansas State University, is offered an ambassadorship by Paul Ellison, the US president. She rejects the offer because her husband, Dr. Edward Ashley, does not want to leave his medical practice, and she is not willing to be separated from him. She also feels that it is harder to find a good doctor for a small Kansas town than an ambassador to a foreign country. When her husband suddenly dies in a traffic accident, Ashley accepts the President's offer in order to fill the void in her life. She is sent to Romania, behind the Iron Curtain, and adapts to the role of ambassador. She takes an instant distaste to her second in command, Mike Slade, but is unable to remove it due to his appointment being a presidential order. Her success as an ambassador turns her into a public face for understanding between the United States and Romania. She begins a relationship with Louis Desforges, a widowed French physician that saves her from attempts to kidnap and poison her, until he gets killed by Slade. nterspeded with that narration, the novel shows gatherings of members of the Patriots for Freedom, a secret society of powerful men that orchestrate political events trying to divide the Eastern and Western Blocs. They hire an international assassin nicknamed Angel to kill her, but the information is leaked and the attempt foiled. In the climax of the novel, it is revealed that Mike Slade is an agent who infiltrated the Patriots for Freedom and foiled their plans, while Desforges was an agent of the Patriots who saved her only so she could be publicly killed by Angel. The members of the Patriots are arrested and their chairman (revealed to be the Vice-president of the United States) is killed by Angel after refusing to pay for the failed assassination.<br /><br />تاریخ نخستین خوانش: سال 1995 میلادی<br />عنوان: آس‍ی‍اب‌ خ‍دای‍ان‌؛ ن‍ویسنده: س‍ی‍دن‍ی‌ ش‍ل‍دون‌؛ مت‍رج‍م: اس‍دال‍ل‍ه‌ طاه‍ری‌؛ ت‍ه‍ران‌: ش‍ب‍اوی‍ز‏‫، 1373؛ در چهار، و 446 ص؛ شابک: 9645511763؛‬ موضوع: داستانهای نویسندگان ایالات متحده آمریکا - سده 20 م<br />عنوان: س‍ف‍ی‍ر؛ نویسنده: س‍ی‍دن‍ی‌ ش‍ل‍دون‌؛ م‍ت‍رج‍م‌: ش‍رف‌ال‍دی‍ن‌ ش‍رف‍ی‌؛ ت‍ه‍ران‌: راس‍ت‍ی‌ ن‍و‏‫، 1381؛ در 544 ص؛ شابک: 9645611156؛‬<br />عنوان: س‍ف‍ی‍رک‍ب‍ی‍ر؛ نویسنده: س‍ی‍دن‍ی‌ ش‍ل‍دون‌ ؛ مترج‍م: م‍ه‍گ‍ون‍ه‌ ق‍ه‍رم‍ان‌؛ ت‍ه‍ران‌ : درس‍ا‏‫ ، 1381؛ در 428 ص؛ شابک: 9646104525؛ چاپ سوم 1386؛‬<br /><br />قرار بود «استنتن راجرز» به ریاست جمهوری ایالات متحد آمریکا برگزیده شود. ایشان سیاستمداری نامدار بودند که در نزد همگی مردمان جایگاهی بزرگ داشتند و دوستان نیرومند ایشان نیز از او حمایت میکردند. و...؛ نقل نمونه ای از متن: «در نویلی ساعت دو بامداد بود. ویلای گروزا در تاریکی فرو رفته بود. سکوت خیابان‌های خاموش و آرام را، گهگاه عبور رهگذری در هم می‌شکست. شبح سیاهپوشی، بی‌سر و صدا به سوی دیوار آجری پیرامون ویلا رفت. بر روی یک شانه یک حلقه طناب و یک پتو و در دست دیگر اسلحه‌ ای حمل می‌کرد. به دیوار رسید و گوش فرا داد. پنج دقیقه تمام صبر کرد و بعد حلقه طناب را باز کرد و قلاب آن را به سوی دیوار انداخت. با اطمینان از استحکام طناب، به آرامی شروع به بالا رفتن کرد. با رسیدن به لبه دیوار، پتویی را که به همراه آورده بود، پهن کرد. قلاب را باز کرد و طناب را از سوی دیگر دیوار پایین فرستاد. از دیوار پایین رفت و هم زمان دست خود را به حالت آماده‌ باش بر روی چاقوی ضامن‌داری که به کمر داشت گذاشت. حالا نوبت رویارویی با سگ‌های نگهبان ویلا بود...؛»؛ پایان نقل. ا. شربیانی</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

<span id="freeTextContainer148800042919844697">It could have been 5 stars but I found the beginning somewhat slow-paced. But the story, as a whole, was good.<br/><br/>I would like to talk about some of the characters...<br/><br/><b>Edward.</b> What happened to him was heartbreaking. An innocent party that took the "fall" for the benefit of others.<br/><br/><b>Groza.</b> Below was what happened to him/his family...<br/><i>"Scenes of his wife and his daughter being raped seared through his brain. It was a gang rape, and the laughing soldiers went from the woman to the child, their pants pulled </i></span>
  <span id="freeText148800042919844697" style="display:none">It could have been 5 stars but I found the beginning somewhat slow-paced. But the story, as a whole, was good.<br><br>I would like to talk about some of the characters...<br><br><b>Edward.</b> What happened to him was heartbreaking. An innocent party that took the "fall" for the benefit of others.<br><br><b>Groza.</b> Below was what happened to him/his family...<br><i>"Scenes of his wife and his daughter being raped seared through his brain. It was a gang rape, and the laughing soldiers went from the woman to the child, their pants pulled down, waiting in line for their turn. Marin Groza strained against the stool as though bound to it. As the whip fell again and again he could hear the screams of his wife and daughter begging for mercy, choking on the men’s<br>penises in their mouths, being raped and sodomized at the same time, until the blood started pouring out and their cries finally trailed off."</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/273240.gif" width="300" height="169" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Harry Lantz.</b> If I remembered it correctly, he was the one having threesome. Well, at least he enjoyed his sex life before he forced himself to bed Nuesca. The distance he would go for money would have been funny if not pathetic. Too bad he wasn't as clever as he thought he was.<br><br><b>Mary Ashley.</b> She proved her worth. Excelled in a place dominated by <i>"male chauvinist pigs".</i> Knows how to play dirty and turn a situation to her benefit. Smart woman. Smart woman until she fell in love. Falling in love was her downfall. Wait. Let me amend that. Falling in love <b>WITH THE WRONG MAN</b> was her downfall. If she intended to trust no one, then she shouldn't make an exception. Emotions cloud judgment. She made herself believe all the things Louis said just because she thought he loves her. What a joke. Sabi nga nung lola ko nung nabubuhay pa sya, <i>"Walang ikalawang glorya".</i> And in this case, I agree with her.<br><br><b>Louis, Mike Slade</b> and <b>Stanton.</b> I am happy with myself. I know this is just a book. That they are just fictional characters but I was freaking glad that I pegged all three of them correctly. Even if what I was reading at a certain moment contradicted with what I thought their characters were, I stood by my assumptions. For <b>Louis</b>, <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380403076ra/783998.gif" width="500" height="268" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>For <b>Mike Slade</b>, <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380403076ra/783999.gif" width="500" height="281" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>And for you, <b>Stanton</b>, <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380376143ra/730902.gif" width="500" height="212" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>All in all, I really, really, REALLY liked it.<br><br>Oh! I forgot someone. <b>Ben Cohn</b>. The ever adorable Ben Cohn. Who the hell name their penis ARTHUR? Why Arthur out of all names? Or, in the first place, why name his penis? He was weird. Too nosy for his own good. And as they say, <i>curiosity killed the cat</i>.<br></span>

            Shelves:

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer1045172328110915765"><b>
  <i>We are all victims Anselmo,<br/>Our destinies are decided<br/>by a cosmic roll of the dice<br/>by the winds of the stars<br/>the vagrant breezes<br/>of fortune that blow from<br/>the windmills of the gods.</i>
</b><br/><br/>As I turned away from my boyfriend's supple arms, I took a book I had read over a million times, with its dog-eared pages and put it aside. And picked another book I decided to reread, Windmills of the Gods, which I had last read in 2010. Having taken 7 years to revisit the book, I thought it would be nice to traverse t</span>
  <span id="freeText1045172328110915765" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>We are all victims Anselmo,<br />Our destinies are decided<br />by a cosmic roll of the dice<br />by the winds of the stars<br />the vagrant breezes<br />of fortune that blow from<br />the windmills of the gods.</i>
</b><br /><br />As I turned away from my boyfriend's supple arms, I took a book I had read over a million times, with its dog-eared pages and put it aside. And picked another book I decided to reread, Windmills of the Gods, which I had last read in 2010. Having taken 7 years to revisit the book, I thought it would be nice to traverse the course of finding these windmills of these gods.<br /><br />However, there were no windmills. And there were no gods. <br /><br />What happened was lots of suspenseful narration about the American ambassador to Romania. There were some assassins, a freedom fighter, some guns, some explosions and some more guns. <br /><br />I enjoyed the hell out of the thrill ride. <br /><br />But upon turning the last page, when I realised that there were no gods I simply put the book away to join the dog-eared library and wondered why they didn't at least add some windmills.</span>

<div id="review_2446066099" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2446066099" />
    <a title="Henry Ozogula" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/60135671-henry-ozogula"><img alt="Henry Ozogula" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1563357588p2/60135671.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2446066099?book_show_action=true">Jul 05, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Henry Ozogula" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Henry Ozogula" href="/user/show/60135671-henry-ozogula">Henry Ozogula</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2446066099" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5284346729501267536"><br/>Another gripping work by Sheldon of course. For me the character of Angel the international assassin remains intriguing, if not quite convincing in the end. It is some sort of masterstroke that the author ensures throughout this work that the reader would imagine that both Angel and Neusa are the same. One eg assumes that Angel would be a man, not a woman. The author writes - a fine sleight of hand really - "First Angel had some shopping to do. There was a good lingerie shop on Pueyrredon, expen</span>
  <span id="freeText5284346729501267536" style="display:none"><br />Another gripping work by Sheldon of course. For me the character of Angel the international assassin remains intriguing, if not quite convincing in the end. It is some sort of masterstroke that the author ensures throughout this work that the reader would imagine that both Angel and Neusa are the same. One eg assumes that Angel would be a man, not a woman. The author writes - a fine sleight of hand really - "First Angel had some shopping to do. There was a good lingerie shop on Pueyrredon, expensive, but Neusa deserved the best". How would the reader suss out here that Angel was actually referring to himself...er, herself! Yet from a critical point of view, the concept does not ring true. Neusa is presented as a very unattractive, illiterate dithering, quite foolish individual; yet in reality she is sophisticated, canny, quite a genius. So maybe we should assume again that she is the greatest actress the World has ever seen with what she pulls off!<br />Mary Ashley, the real female protagonist of this work finds herself trapped in a diabolic international plot… which sees those she believes are very much on her side propelling her towards a terrible fate. But at least the ruthless 'Controller' in the end is not only decapitated, but has his eyes torn out…hmmm….<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5284346729501267536" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/342773706?book_show_action=true">Jun 05, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sully (thysaltymar)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sully (thysaltymar)" href="/user/show/9986049-sully-thysaltymar">Sully (thysaltymar)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9986049-sully-thysaltymar?shelf=favorite">favorite</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9986049-sully-thysaltymar?shelf=owned-books">owned-books</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer342773706" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12934824553634092997">I think I just forgot how to spell the word OSM (as in the impression saying how you were extremely impressed and inspired with great admiration to something, apprehension/ def: extremely good; excellent) because this book is more than just OSM. *crying, tears of joy* lol. :))<br/><br/>Anyway, setting that emotion and the feeling that my <i>mind-has-been-"Sheldonized"</i> aside (hahaha). Windmills of the Gods is a 1987 thriller novel written by my all-time favorite American writer (shall I say his name uh-gain? </span>
  <span id="freeText12934824553634092997" style="display:none">I think I just forgot how to spell the word OSM (as in the impression saying how you were extremely impressed and inspired with great admiration to something, apprehension/ def: extremely good; excellent) because this book is more than just OSM. *crying, tears of joy* lol. :))<br /><br />Anyway, setting that emotion and the feeling that my <i>mind-has-been-"Sheldonized"</i> aside (hahaha). Windmills of the Gods is a 1987 thriller novel written by my all-time favorite American writer (shall I say his name uh-gain? yep! Sidney Sheldon). I think Sheldon defied the laws approvingly in writing this book! Hoho. It’s a story about the world where Iron Curtain still exists (overtly, of course ;). Back from the end of World War II in 1945 until the end of the Cold War in 1991, Iron Curtain was utilized to separate the ideological conflict and physical boundary dividing Europe, hence, the democratic sphere and the communist sphere was thoroughly divided. Windmills of the Gods, on the other hand, is a story under the "Iron Curtain days" where the utmost concern of the United States to Eastern Europe bloc (particularly in Romania) was fictionally discussed. And damn it was overly intriguing, heart-thrilling and mind-boggling!<br /><br />The first situation that appealed me is when Sheldon introduced a beautiful and accomplished scholar who has suddenly became the newest United States ambassador to an Iron Curtain country, a woman who is about to dramatically change the course of world events. Imagine how her pretty face could survive on the glinting edge of East-West confrontation. <br /><br />Every chapter is exceptionally impressive. Exceptionally and excessively impressive. <br /><br />This novel grabbed me with all its all-sort of cliff-hangers, hooks and everything that come with it and finished read it in just one-sitting. RECOMMENDED!!! *__*</span>
  <a data-text-id="12934824553634092997" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText11733682754123359175" style="display:none">This is actually my favorite SS book. It wasn't as dynamic or surprising as the other books he have written but there is something in it that draws you. This book felt so different from the other books he had written. I mean different. Like isolated LOL. Anyway teh plot is great! kinda ordinary compared to some of his works that went extreme (in a great wayh) but as gripping as the others<br /> <br />I thnk the fact that the pro and the man never kissed or made love increased the excitement. I was waiting for them to kiss or hold hands but they never did; it was almost...innocent and i think that made me like it 10 times more. I love the man (forgot the name, i tend not to remember the chars name after reading a book), the dark and sexy aura he has, and it was described in a magnificent way; like your watching him yourself, like you can touch him and talk to him. <br /><br />The girl wasnt my fave heroine but i did care about her. The story is intense, i finished it in a just a few hours.The way SS write his books are always as smooth as a silk and seemed so effortless.He writes with such simpleness that makes you think he has written the book in just a few weeks, published it then viola made millions of dollors, thats how smooth and well-woven it is. <br /><br /></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1637873444" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9644801808370066657">When the US President calls Mary Ashley, a university professor to offer an ambassadorship to a country she was attached to, Romania, she surprises herself refusing the offer. Her husband is practicing medicine and moving to another country without his and the children, isn't worth any dreams. <br/><br/>But after her husband's sudden and mysterious death, she isn't left with any choice other than accepting the ambassadorship. She comes under the public's scrutinizing gaze, never allowed to make mistakes, </span>
  <span id="freeText9644801808370066657" style="display:none">When the US President calls Mary Ashley, a university professor to offer an ambassadorship to a country she was attached to, Romania, she surprises herself refusing the offer. Her husband is practicing medicine and moving to another country without his and the children, isn't worth any dreams. <br /><br />But after her husband's sudden and mysterious death, she isn't left with any choice other than accepting the ambassadorship. She comes under the public's scrutinizing gaze, never allowed to make mistakes, her every move being noted and meticulously inspected. She never thought her job could be a turning point in her life. Soon, her life is in danger, from forces she doesn't understand. Her decision to write history seems trivial when the matter is of life and death. <br /><br />This is one of those books that will uplift your mood, just to praise how intelligent and dedicated patriotic the protagonist was. Her knowledge and interest in Romanian culture can inspire anyone. </span>

This is how we go on.” <br />― Sidney Sheldon, Windmills of the Gods<br /><br /><br /><br /><br />Another good Sheldon book. <span id="freeTextContainer16159621494054596595">Yet another great story from Sidney Sheldon. <br/><br/>His stories are fun, entertaining reads that I look forward to. <br/><br/>"Windmills" is a Cold War era thriller with plot lines that still resonate in the post 9/11 world.<br/><br/>While reading this, I thought of events that happened in Eastern Europe a few years ago. These events were perfect bookends to what happened in "Windmills".<br/><br/>Sheldon's stories in some respects are eerily becoming true.<br/><br/></span>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText14938426923562347928" style="display:none">Marie Ashley a beautiful young lady, teacher of the Cansas state University.who is specialist of "Eastern Europe" countries. New USA president wants to improve relationship with the communist countries. So he decides to nominate Marie Ashley as the ambassador of the Romania. As Marie starts her job in Romania she finds that she isn't liked by many for colleague and she has also got some powerful enemies who wants erase her for good."Angel" who is considered one of the best assassin is hired by hidden community who wants to destroy the people to people program and for that they have to kill Marie Ashley.Not the best work of Sidney Sheldon but still this book offers much to the thriller lovers. Divided into small chapter which is the speciality  of Sidney sheldon and makes the book more enjoyable. I will give 1/2 marks more because of the last twist.         <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2596925189" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer5173756797751495239">The world's seventh best selling author hits the right chords with WINDMILLS OF THE GODS! Not only does he take you around the world, painting vivid pictures of the cities duly mentioned, but also provides the readers with informative political scenarios, coupled with 'his' fair share of crime and drama.<br/><br/>The Writer cleverly enmeshes the opaque "political underworld" to the glim picture he paints of the apprehensions of the communist countries, towards the United States, and vice versa. The workin</span>
  <span id="freeText5173756797751495239" style="display:none">The world's seventh best selling author hits the right chords with WINDMILLS OF THE GODS! Not only does he take you around the world, painting vivid pictures of the cities duly mentioned, but also provides the readers with informative political scenarios, coupled with 'his' fair share of crime and drama.<br /><br />The Writer cleverly enmeshes the opaque "political underworld" to the glim picture he paints of the apprehensions of the communist countries, towards the United States, and vice versa. The workings of a diplomat have been put in with incredible care (and in great detail)... And the tenacious, amiable, and homely nature of the protagonist is certain to win you over. Each of the characters have been sketched with utmost ambiguity and ONE amongst them, in particular, is certain to knock you off your feet!<br /><br />The book overall may not possibly touch you emotionally (which i do not think it intended to), but will leave you highly satisfied and with a smile on your face! Keeping in mind the amount of declassified information available today, and the number of clandestine operations the governments of the modern world are involved in, Sidney Sheldon and this book remain all the more relevant.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5173756797751495239" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/305217757?book_show_action=true">Apr 02, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kelly" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kelly" href="/user/show/8545345-kelly">Kelly</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8545345-kelly?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8545345-kelly?shelf=crime-thrillers-and-mystery">crime-thrillers-and-mystery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer305217757" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2612262170910601333">This novel was spilt into three 'books' with the second and third being a lot better than the first. <br/><br/>The first 'book' was setting up the whole novel and plot, this was fine, but I felt that it was a bit too disjointed. It jumped from one person to the other and then back, there were a series of names that I couldn't keep track of, different political terms and affiliations, relationship and sub-plots.<br/><br/>By the second book I had pinned down who everyone was and actually realised that the first book,</span>
  <span id="freeText2612262170910601333" style="display:none">This novel was spilt into three 'books' with the second and third being a lot better than the first. <br /><br />The first 'book' was setting up the whole novel and plot, this was fine, but I felt that it was a bit too disjointed. It jumped from one person to the other and then back, there were a series of names that I couldn't keep track of, different political terms and affiliations, relationship and sub-plots.<br /><br />By the second book I had pinned down who everyone was and actually realised that the first book, though not entirely action packed, had nicely set me up for the impact of the second and third. We began to see a development in Mary's character and she became our primary narrator, and this was where the novel came into its own.<br /><br />Mary was like most of Sheldon's female narrators, strong, independent and incredibly compelling. Once she had me hooked on her story I just couldn't stop reading. There were times when I was sympathising with her, shouting angrily at her, laughing with her... but she had me with her the whole time. <br /><br />I read 457 in about four hours, and Lord help me, but when it finished I <i> needed </i> more! <br /><br />Not just a good read, but a brilliant read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2612262170910601333" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer152885201" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer13479773212349400647">How a story is presented in the beginning, middle, & end is an essential factor that keeps the readers of into pages. Sidney Sheldon did it well on his Windmills of the Gods, & successfully placed a strong ingredient that surprises readers every now & then. The pacing is perfect. The plot is excellent. The story itself is well-researched. Windmills of the Gods is one of the greatest suspense stories I've had read, and Sidney Sheldon succeeded in hooking me up with such a breath-taking story, a f</span>
  <span id="freeText13479773212349400647" style="display:none">How a story is presented in the beginning, middle, &amp; end is an essential factor that keeps the readers of into pages. Sidney Sheldon did it well on his Windmills of the Gods, &amp; successfully placed a strong ingredient that surprises readers every now &amp; then. The pacing is perfect. The plot is excellent. The story itself is well-researched. Windmills of the Gods is one of the greatest suspense stories I've had read, and Sidney Sheldon succeeded in hooking me up with such a breath-taking story, a fast-paced journey unto the world of politics &amp; its darkest mysteries, the hidden risks behind intellect &amp; fame, the roller coaster ride to the international secrets, sex &amp; murder at their worst, a family at danger in every choice to take, and the survival amidst greedy interests and deceits in a game of life. There's only a few writers who can bring it on; and Sidney Sheldon is one worth to get such prestige.</span>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer7771070658607948795">The characters in this book are compelling and keep you on your toes. <br/><br/>One thing I didn't like about this book though, is it seemed to constantly jump all over the place. Not that it was hard to keep track of everything though. <br/><br/>I was quite surprised at the end when Mike turned out to be the good guy! That caught me completely off guard. I was truly hoping Stanton would be the man he had been portrayed as, also, but that wasn't the case, either! Everyone in this book wasn't who they seemed to be!<br/><br/>I</span>
  <span id="freeText7771070658607948795" style="display:none">The characters in this book are compelling and keep you on your toes. <br /><br />One thing I didn't like about this book though, is it seemed to constantly jump all over the place. Not that it was hard to keep track of everything though. <br /><br />I was quite surprised at the end when Mike turned out to be the good guy! That caught me completely off guard. I was truly hoping Stanton would be the man he had been portrayed as, also, but that wasn't the case, either! Everyone in this book wasn't who they seemed to be!<br /><br />I enjoyed it though. Anyone who is a Sheldon fan should definitely add this one to their collection.</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3382827510" />
    <a title="AqeelReads" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/42704015-aqeelreads"><img alt="AqeelReads" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1590138082p2/42704015.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3382827510?book_show_action=true">Jul 15, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="AqeelReads" class="user" itemprop="url" name="AqeelReads" href="/user/show/42704015-aqeelreads">AqeelReads</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3382827510" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7425101448139791502">Sidney Sheldon knows how to culminate a thriller book for sure.<br/>Let's take it from the very beginning, the book is averagely good till we get to Romania. Building up of the characters is good; not the best to be honest, creating suspense has been tried really hard without much success. First half of the book can be read when there is nothing much to read but it isn't something to admire, something to think about. Latter half of the book is where the twists and turns really start to come. Honestly</span>
  <span id="freeText7425101448139791502" style="display:none">Sidney Sheldon knows how to culminate a thriller book for sure.<br />Let's take it from the very beginning, the book is averagely good till we get to Romania. Building up of the characters is good; not the best to be honest, creating suspense has been tried really hard without much success. First half of the book can be read when there is nothing much to read but it isn't something to admire, something to think about. Latter half of the book is where the twists and turns really start to come. Honestly, an avid reader can tell who is behind what long before it's revealed in the book but believe me it won't tarnish the climax. The ending, the 'dessert' of the book is quite nice. Fine, it good. Alright its one of the best endings I have ever read. This book gets one extra star because of that ending.<br /><br />Read it only if you are patient enough to wait for the ending.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7425101448139791502" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ahrVBjVyw04aelOwXD5/BQYTssNNzvVM7XNYswMIBFxDF3iCvbn6K233MGk4Kp476KbICoVPe6j6k8EAay2GRg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ouUxidr/Jw6yn9Cw5b/SRmrik3FpJNMmbss6S/wyNDKL6JwNUjQea8USs2mBqzN4hFfpuKGlXcJ5K6P4lBe2KA==')})
  }

Teddy--Maggy\'s  daughter, the incomparable cover girl who lived fast  and left as her legacy Mistral\'s dazzling love  child. <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer13631276416095705021">Sidney Sheldon (1917-2007) was an American writer who won awards in three careers—a Broadway playwright, a Hollywood TV and movie screenwriter, and a best-selling novelist.<br/><br/>His TV works spanned a twenty-year period during which he created <i>I Dream of Jeannie</i> (1965-70), <i>Hart to Hart</i> (1979-84), and <i>The Patty Duke Show</i> (1963-66), but it was not until after he turned 50 and began writing best-selling no</span>
  <span id="freeText13631276416095705021" style="display:none">Sidney Sheldon (1917-2007) was an American writer who won awards in three careers—a Broadway playwright, a Hollywood TV and movie screenwriter, and a best-selling novelist.<br /><br />His TV works spanned a twenty-year period during which he created <i>I Dream of Jeannie</i> (1965-70), <i>Hart to Hart</i> (1979-84), and <i>The Patty Duke Show</i> (1963-66), but it was not until after he turned 50 and began writing best-selling novels such as <i>Master of the Game</i> (1982), <i>The Other Side of Midnight</i> (1973) and <i>Rage of Angels</i> (1980) that he became most famous.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13631276416095705021" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
